  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

<div id="review_1046097221" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1046097221" />
    <a title="Natalie Vellacott" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/34178791-natalie-vellacott"><img alt="Natalie Vellacott" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442984500p2/34178791.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1046097221?book_show_action=true">Sep 05, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Natalie Vellacott" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Natalie Vellacott" href="/user/show/34178791-natalie-vellacott">Natalie Vellacott</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34178791-natalie-vellacott?shelf=christian-biography">christian-biography</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1046097221" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14233571748015987760">I hate to do this to another classic, but I have to be honest. This was an extremely popular book in Christian circles when I was in my teens (the 1990's.) I read it several times back then and as a relatively new believer probably would have rated it highly. I wondered if my perspective had changed so got hold of a free copy and re-read it now, well some of it.<br/><br/>There is no doubt that the story itself is an incredible working of God's power in the life of gangster Nicky Cruz through His servant D</span>
  <span id="freeText14233571748015987760" style="display:none">I hate to do this to another classic, but I have to be honest. This was an extremely popular book in Christian circles when I was in my teens (the 1990's.) I read it several times back then and as a relatively new believer probably would have rated it highly. I wondered if my perspective had changed so got hold of a free copy and re-read it now, well some of it.<br /><br />There is no doubt that the story itself is an incredible working of God's power in the life of gangster Nicky Cruz through His servant David Wilkerson. I remember also reading <i>The Cross and the Switchblade</i> which tells the story from Wilkerson's point of view. There is also a film which I watched once....<br /><br />However, this time of reading, I was appalled by the gratuitous violence and the graphic descriptions of it. I stopped reading at the point where the gang deal with a failed recruit by stabbing him in both armpits. I appreciate that the turn-around in Cruz' life was more miraculous due to the level of depravity he had reached and that that is one of the reasons why the details have been included. But, reading it now as a (hopefully) more spiritually mature adult, it is truly sickening. I can't believe I read it as a teen and wasn't unduly bothered by the violence.<br /><br />I reviewed <i>Street God</i> last year with a one star rating due to the author appearing to glorify sin in his testimony. (<a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://christianmissionaryuk.blogspot.co.uk/2016/05/writing-with-purpose-or-glorifying-sin.html">http://christianmissionaryuk.blogspot...</a>) Honestly, there is little difference between the two books in terms of the graphic nature. <i>Street God</i> probably contains a lot more detail of drug abuse but <i>Run Baby Run</i> has sexual details that shocked me and that I didn't recall from my first reading all those years ago.<br /><br />Either I have become a legalist as I have grown older in which case feel free to disregard my review or sanctification is actually changing me albeit slowly and I can no longer tolerate things that would have been acceptable to me in the past. The Bible suggests it is probably the latter...<br /><br />I can't recommend this book, it is full of graphic violence and some sexual content as well as shortened versions of bad language.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14233571748015987760" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_45119885" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/45119885" />
    <a title="Ilze" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1147966-ilze"><img alt="Ilze" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1477553914p2/1147966.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/45119885?book_show_action=true">Feb 02, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ilze" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ilze" href="/user/show/1147966-ilze">Ilze</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780340861967" href="/book/show/241825.Run_Baby_Run">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer45119885" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18309154779461551203">Having read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/772852.The_Cross_and_the_Switchblade' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Cross and the Switchblade</a> as well as <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2597907.Lonely_but_Never_Alone' rel='nofollow noopener'>Lonely but Never Alone</a> in 1990, I thought I knew the story well enough not to still bother with "Run Baby Run". I mean, if you've heard it once, you've heard it all ... besides, I couldn't get hold of this book at our local library then. <br/><br/>But I was wrong. This book reveals far more details of Cruz' life before he ran away from home - here you have his motivations and start to understand his fear once he's the leader of the Mau Maus. In fact, it</span>
  <span id="freeText18309154779461551203" style="display:none">Having read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/772852.The_Cross_and_the_Switchblade" rel="nofollow noopener">The Cross and the Switchblade</a> as well as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2597907.Lonely_but_Never_Alone" rel="nofollow noopener">Lonely but Never Alone</a> in 1990, I thought I knew the story well enough not to still bother with "Run Baby Run". I mean, if you've heard it once, you've heard it all ... besides, I couldn't get hold of this book at our local library then. <br /><br />But I was wrong. This book reveals far more details of Cruz' life before he ran away from home - here you have his motivations and start to understand his fear once he's the leader of the Mau Maus. In fact, it might be a very good idea to go back to the other books I mentioned and read them again - "<i>The Cross and the Switchblade</i>" being Wilkerson's view of that ghetto and Nicky's conversion. God walks with those He loves.<br /><br />PS Someone like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1410631.The_Killing_Jar" rel="nofollow noopener">Kez (and Mark)</a> needs to get to one of their outreaches.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18309154779461551203" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17074256296603256111">I really enjoyed this book and read it twice. I would read it again. It is very well written and it's a page turner. For anyone who likes Cross and the Switchblade, this is the book for you.<br/><br/>The bulk of the book is about Nicky's experience in the gang called Mau-Maus. Truthfully, the kid was a terror and that's putting it mildly. The stage is set.   <span id="freeText17074256296603256111" style="display:none">I really enjoyed this book and read it twice. I would read it again. It is very well written and it's a page turner. For anyone who likes Cross and the Switchblade, this is the book for you.<br /><br />The bulk of the book is about Nicky's experience in the gang called Mau-Maus. Truthfully, the kid was a terror and that's putting it mildly. The stage is set. Nicky was a ruthless violent thug, the police were scared of him and he was pretty much immune to reprisal. <br /><br />Enter David Wilkerson, skinny preacher. David presented Jesus and afterwards, Nicky was never the same. The second half of the book is how Nicky became a preacher and helped go back to the streets he had grown up in during Teen Challenge's formative years.<br /><br />For anyone looking for a book about the life changing power of the Gospel of Jesus Christ, this is the book. <br /><br />The only negative thing I can say about the book is that Nicky placed a big emphasis on the Baptism of the Holy Spirit in the modern day, which I really don't know that I agree with for reasons I will avoid here. He also had some sort of connection to Kathryn Kuhlmann who was almost like the Benny Hinn of her day. So with those two facts, I would advise readers to proceed with caution, exercise Acts 17:11 and proper discernment. I'm not dpubting Nicky's salvation, just advising to be careful if you are a young Christian. This book did help me in some ways, but it also had some stuff that I felt was not right for me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17074256296603256111" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText9261758058182240264" style="display:none">One of the best books I have ever read. Even after several re-reads this book still leaves me speechless. <br /><br />This is the story of Nicky Cruz, a misunderstood teenager from Puerto Rico who finds himself the leader of one of the most notorious gangs of New York, the Mau-Maus. Struggling with the lifestyle of a warlord, fighting gangs, killing, stealing, drugs, sex and much more. He stumbles upon a preacher, David Wilkerson. Soon Nicky's eyes are open and his life goes down a different path.<br /><br />This powerful story of a boy that develops and grows into one of the most influential Christian leaders in the world is a unique, heart wrenching story. <br /><br />This book is one of those powerful books that will stay with you forever. <span id="freeTextContainer6384640367580267332">Wow. What makes this book hard to read is the violence and language. The book tells a testimony of a reputable gang leader of one of NYC’s most violent gang members in the 50’s. He is explicit in his telling of crimes and his use of foul language and racial slurs. He admits that he was full of fear, hate, and sin. You could argue the point in how he could use that language and use such violent detail as a redeemed person. I don’t think he was trying to glorify his sin, but paint the picture for </span>
  <span id="freeText6384640367580267332" style="display:none">Wow. What makes this book hard to read is the violence and language. The book tells a testimony of a reputable gang leader of one of NYC’s most violent gang members in the 50’s. He is explicit in his telling of crimes and his use of foul language and racial slurs. He admits that he was full of fear, hate, and sin. You could argue the point in how he could use that language and use such violent detail as a redeemed person. I don’t think he was trying to glorify his sin, but paint the picture for what it was -full of fear, hate, and sin - and to get a beautiful picture of God’s forgiveness. Nevertheless, maybe he could have done that in a better way. You decide. If you can get past the language and violence, you find an amazing story of redemption. God loves, and can change the worst of the worst into a beacon for his glory. I’m glad I don’t have a past like his, but I want his love, devotion, and boldness for God.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6384640367580267332" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2422960002" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer4594176304127725062">Run Baby Run is one of the best books I've read written by a Christian, and without a doubt, one of the best books I have yet to read. <br/><br/>It's a powerful testimony of a man whose hardened heart could only be broken through by relentless love. The main character, Nicky Cruz, started life out bitter and angry, having been born into a family who practiced witchcraft. He hit the streets of New York City at fifteen, thieving, drinking, attacking, and it wasn't three years later when his life changed in </span>
  <span id="freeText4594176304127725062" style="display:none">Run Baby Run is one of the best books I've read written by a Christian, and without a doubt, one of the best books I have yet to read. <br /><br />It's a powerful testimony of a man whose hardened heart could only be broken through by relentless love. The main character, Nicky Cruz, started life out bitter and angry, having been born into a family who practiced witchcraft. He hit the streets of New York City at fifteen, thieving, drinking, attacking, and it wasn't three years later when his life changed in a drastic way. <br />There was so much hurt buried in Cruz's heart, that it allowed the reader to resonate to a degree, while still his sins could not be excused. There was so much love, and light that came afterwards when he came to Christ. Though it's necessary to say things didn't become automatically easy for him in the aftermath. <br /><br /> I did have a few doubts when I realized the ministries and characters, involved were mainly Pentecostal, as I come from a middle class family, and was raised in a non-denominational <br />setting. While I wouldn't discount the things I've learned from the church, I feel there were spiritual aspects seldom mentioned. The power of the Holy Spirit, or the work of the enemy -constantly working at tearing us down. Spiritual warfare itself, though usually, it's hardly spoken of among Christians I know. <br />And while I'm sure this isn't always the case with all Evangelical and Non denominational Christians, Run Baby Run reminded me that there is a tremendous battle being waged. It reminded me that there is a great evil that can manifest itself in many ways, and trying to self medicate will not solve anything. That we can not be so intent on fitting in that we forget that this is not our home. Out hearts and minds must be transformed, renewed by the Holy Spirit.<br /><br /> To put it briefly, this book is about redemption, relational redemption, and being bought back, paid for to be free. Nicky Cruz was a man who would have never thought to love, a killer, a gangster, but the seriously overwhelming, never ending love of God changed that. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4594176304127725062" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Justin Rose" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Justin Rose" href="/user/show/12693827-justin-rose">Justin Rose</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer784380919" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17410686167380699482">Cruz may have some good and inspiring stories to tell, but he adds too much circumstance under the auspices of divine intervention. I think in Latin American this kind of story telling is accepted, but in English speaking America, this comes across as patronizing. Mike Warnke's /The Satan Seller/ is in this same genre, but it takes knowledge outside the text to see the inconsistencies.<br/><br/>Another thing that would have made this book better is if Cruz concentrated on a few stories in detail, rather t</span>
  <span id="freeText17410686167380699482" style="display:none">Cruz may have some good and inspiring stories to tell, but he adds too much circumstance under the auspices of divine intervention. I think in Latin American this kind of story telling is accepted, but in English speaking America, this comes across as patronizing. Mike Warnke's /The Satan Seller/ is in this same genre, but it takes knowledge outside the text to see the inconsistencies.<br /><br />Another thing that would have made this book better is if Cruz concentrated on a few stories in detail, rather than a lot of stories briefly. He talks about drug addiction so passively that it is hard to believe that he was an integral part of that culture.<br /><br />Finally, Cruz presents an unbiblical understanding of the grace of God. Over and over he presents being healed from drug addiction as the result of people laying hands on the addict's head while praying. While this does happen, it is an exceptional miracle, not an expected result as Cruz makes it sound. Such miracles demonstrate God's grace, but his grace is more vividly displayed when Jesus accepts people into his fold who are sick, who have trouble remembering their friends' first names, who still burn with that physical urge for inebriation.<br /><br />Another area where Cruz has an unbiblical (even cultish) understanding of God's grace is the Pentecostal movement's understanding of the filling of the Holy Spirit. His idea that there is a second filling of the Holy Spirit makes this experience dependent on man's work, not God's grace. And his connotations of the gift of tongues demonstrate spiritual gifts of the devil, not of the Holy Spirit.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17410686167380699482" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText7961272399977837347" style="display:none">Run baby run, a brilliant thrilling book of the true story of Nicky Cruz.   <span id="freeText9513328401194159762" style="display:none"><b>RUN BABY RUN</b> • by Nicky Cruz, with Jamie Buckingham.<br /><br />Nicky Cruz was born &amp; raised in Puerto Rico, living in one of the worst neighborhoods. He eventually accepts the gospel of Christ and gives up his gang life, crime &amp; violence.<br /><br />You can find the other side of the story in the book, "The Cross and the Switchblade," by David Wilkerson.<br /><br />Both are remarkable biographies--frightening &amp; hopeful.</span>

<div id="review_2921687" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2921687" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17563415432957444407">This was one of my favorite books when I was a teenager, and is still one I hold dear. It is the autobiography of Nicky Cruz, a character in the Cross and the Switchblade, by David Wilkerson. Nicky was a haunted and angry young man, sent away by his family in Puerto Ricko to the slums of New York City in the 60s. This is the story of his life with the gangs, from his start to his rise to the top, and his dramatic meeting with God through the unlikely skinny little preacher from Pennsylvania. Thi</span>
  <span id="freeText17563415432957444407" style="display:none">This was one of my favorite books when I was a teenager, and is still one I hold dear. It is the autobiography of Nicky Cruz, a character in the Cross and the Switchblade, by David Wilkerson. Nicky was a haunted and angry young man, sent away by his family in Puerto Ricko to the slums of New York City in the 60s. This is the story of his life with the gangs, from his start to his rise to the top, and his dramatic meeting with God through the unlikely skinny little preacher from Pennsylvania. This book was amazing to me as a teenager, reading about how low people can fall, and how high God can raise them up. it's a reminder to us never to give up on someone, because with God are things are possible.<br />spoiler: Nicky is now an internationally crusading urban evangelist. what a difference God can make in a life!</span>
  <a data-text-id="17563415432957444407" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Marja Verschoor-Meijers" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4317542-marja-verschoor-meijers"><img alt="Marja Verschoor-Meijers" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528351405p2/4317542.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/174175440?book_show_action=true">Jun 06, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Marja Verschoor-Meijers" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Marja Verschoor-Meijers" href="/user/show/4317542-marja-verschoor-meijers">Marja Verschoor-Meijers</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer174175440" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13142950972591162354">After reading the Cross and the switchblade I had to read this one. What an incredible story of redemption! If God can change a man like Nicky Cruz, He can change anyone, there is no doubt in my mind. Although this book was very graphic and detailed about all the crimes the gang members committed, it was a good read. it made Nicky's salvation all the more a miracle!</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1890946509" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1890946509" />
    <a title="Sarah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9330937-sarah"><img alt="Sarah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1420172264p2/9330937.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1890946509?book_show_action=true">Feb 06, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah" href="/user/show/9330937-sarah">Sarah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1890946509" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8824063947614463379">I received this book from my grandmother years ago. Quit possibly a few years after my Papa passed. I wanted it because it was old and falling apart, and the cover looked intriguing. I was into collecting books then. I've had it for at least 14 or 15yrs. I had never read it, but kept it for sentimental reasons. Due to some life changes it became part of my need to read and then discard pile. I no longer collect books, just keeping those that bring joy. Again, I picked up the book from my mountai</span>
  <span id="freeText8824063947614463379" style="display:none">I received this book from my grandmother years ago. Quit possibly a few years after my Papa passed. I wanted it because it was old and falling apart, and the cover looked intriguing. I was into collecting books then. I've had it for at least 14 or 15yrs. I had never read it, but kept it for sentimental reasons. Due to some life changes it became part of my need to read and then discard pile. I no longer collect books, just keeping those that bring joy. Again, I picked up the book from my mountain because of the cover. I thought it would be some fiction thing as I didn't want to deal with my 'Jesus books' I've started and stopped. <br /><br />This book surprised me in all the right ways. I went into it thinking, 'oh yeah, another true life account. What snore fest bull lies ahead?'. Imagine my surprise when I was pulled in. This was not my normal read. I was reading it because of sentimental reasons. I couldn't just toss it. Then the life described in the beginning was fascinating and scary. Very scary that not much has changed. It was some insight into a world I was too afraid to go into, but was curious about. Then came the change. Yes, I was like Nicky at that point. Waiting to see it fail. Not expecting to see the fear. The part that got me though was when Nicky was struggling with the Holy Spirit. I went through that journey 11yrs ago. I didn't get what anyone was talking about. I remember the frustration. The tip of the tongue thing that didn't quite make fruition. That 'ah-ha' moment where you were instantly filled to the brim with fullness. There, but just out of reach. My brain was screaming on what he had to do. Then faltered to remember my own experience. It's different for each of us. And it doesn't make sense or happen until God wants it to.<br /><br />I found a renewed spirit in that moment. I have been away for a while. God is still guiding me, and I still pray, and try to remember to place my faith in him. But there is lacking. A clearing is happening which is probably why I wasn't able to just get rid of this book and decided to read it when I did. But I also found that this book brings me joy and it is now getting a new place on my book shelf. I one day hope to pass this story on to my children to show that God is much greater than we believe.<br /><br />I'm so glad it's also written in a way that is not preaching, but from the gut. I didn't feel like it was meant to convert, but to educate. To provide a choice and say 'hey. No matter what, you have the choice on where to go from here.' I highly recommend this to anyone and everyone. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8824063947614463379" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3211483914" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3211483914" />
    <a title="Nicky" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/81869600-nicky"><img alt="Nicky" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528304645p2/81869600.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3211483914?book_show_action=true">Feb 29, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nicky" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nicky" href="/user/show/81869600-nicky">Nicky</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3211483914" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16187327966217005756">I can appreciate the weight of the story of this novel, but as a woman reading it in 2020, it’s painful to read sections where the woman is palmed off as a prop to the mans incessant ego. <br/>This reminds me so much of the novel Shantaram, in how the hero wins in all scrapes, always has the world looking out for him, and even in his blackest hour is the hero! It just doesn’t smack of reality. <br/>It’s a story where you want to support Nicky, and you clap loudly for him when he achieves a change, but the</span>
  <span id="freeText16187327966217005756" style="display:none">I can appreciate the weight of the story of this novel, but as a woman reading it in 2020, it’s painful to read sections where the woman is palmed off as a prop to the mans incessant ego. <br />This reminds me so much of the novel Shantaram, in how the hero wins in all scrapes, always has the world looking out for him, and even in his blackest hour is the hero! It just doesn’t smack of reality. <br />It’s a story where you want to support Nicky, and you clap loudly for him when he achieves a change, but the ego just keeps getting in the way, so the cheering just grinds slowly to a halt as it’s just tooo much selling of oneself. It really is like reading a 240 page sales pitch of someone’s amazing ness than a selfless story related to god. <br /><br />The sentence that really made it apparent it’s a novel of its time is on page 230 ‘later that same month Dave Carter joined our staff to work with the boys.... we also had two young Mexican girls, frances Ramirez &amp; Angie Sedillos, join us to add a woman’s touch and help with secretarial work’. <br /><br />This paragraph was the icing on the cake for destroying my whole enjoyment for the the book. It’s a mans story of a mans world, and it’s pretty 2D egocentric, where the women are props to the mans ego - soft, gentle, sweet (this term is used a lot to describe the women) - or they are sexual play things to be discarded as the man continues his quest with God! <br /><br />For instance, Nicky’s first girlfriend was a self professed Christian and then she was just dropped out the narrative. <br /><br />If any novel I’ve ever read sets out to give an actual woman a complex about being noble for being human with strong, bombastic emotions, sharp intelligence and owning her world she moves in then this is. I mean what is Gloria’s story all about????<br /><br />I think if this novel is going to have legs with the modern world it’s seriously going to have to edit how the women are situated &amp; explained within this story.<br /><br />If I was a man, I probably wouldn’t notice any of the misogyny.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16187327966217005756" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11423729-rosy?shelf=spirituality">spirituality</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11423729-rosy?shelf=violent">violent</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11423729-rosy?shelf=new-york-city">new-york-city</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2046252671" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18376608524699297419">A surprising confluence: I'm going through Christian Wiman's "Ambition and Survival" with the intention of reading all or most of the poets and poems he discusses. That is why I reread "Paradise Lost" earlier this year. In a memoir section Wiman mentions that as a kid "Run Baby Run" was one of his favorite books for a while, and for a short time in my late teens, it was certainly one of mine. Not only that, but it was reissued this April, so I read this one in short order this week. <br/><br/>Turns out I </span>
  <span id="freeText18376608524699297419" style="display:none">A surprising confluence: I'm going through Christian Wiman's "Ambition and Survival" with the intention of reading all or most of the poets and poems he discusses. That is why I reread "Paradise Lost" earlier this year. In a memoir section Wiman mentions that as a kid "Run Baby Run" was one of his favorite books for a while, and for a short time in my late teens, it was certainly one of mine. Not only that, but it was reissued this April, so I read this one in short order this week. <br /><br />Turns out I remembered almost nothing but the broad outline. The first half is so violent! I mean graphically, horridly violent (bearing in mind that it is not fiction). The second half is moving and challenging in the way I would expect it to be, and although the style is inevitably dated, it is still quite an astonishing (and honest) testimony/memoir. This (Kindle) version ended somewhat abruptly, and I have not bothered with more than a cursory glance at the epilogue matter.<br /><br />One observation I found interesting this time around: Some of Cruz's comments about the churches in the late 1950s reminded me that the Jesus Movement had not happened yet and that this book was of course one of the sparks that got that fire going.<br /><br />Good to go back here. Not sure that I will again, but it's on my Kindle, so who knows.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18376608524699297419" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4083742338426903289">I’ve read this book so many times I don’t think I could ever forget it. From humble beginnings as a poor kid growing up in Puerto Rico, to a lonely teen living on New York City streets, to a redeemed man of faith looking to provide the same hope that was offered to him, Nicky Cruz truly transformed his life and made something beautiful from ashes. <br/><br/>Some of the moments are very hard to read, gruesome and violent and difficult to wrap your head around, but so necessary in order to grow that hope th</span>
  <span id="freeText4083742338426903289" style="display:none">I’ve read this book so many times I don’t think I could ever forget it. From humble beginnings as a poor kid growing up in Puerto Rico, to a lonely teen living on New York City streets, to a redeemed man of faith looking to provide the same hope that was offered to him, Nicky Cruz truly transformed his life and made something beautiful from ashes. <br /><br />Some of the moments are very hard to read, gruesome and violent and difficult to wrap your head around, but so necessary in order to grow that hope that he would eventually bring to others who lived similar lives. It’s hard to argue with someone who has walked in your shoes and come out the other side a better person. <br /><br />Having read this book as many times as I have, it becomes increasingly more apparent how everyone is capable of breaking free of their past. <br /><br />🌸</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('vuoRX/Prbh6eSWP1s9LmAysjLD+XhW4wHAabCbzC0IFFK1dkAZMtSdJyG49BBRh6DkzeadTGyg3VcB8fY0Todg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('GVEwYmy5mzLx3ndij9nEHyBM3AcnYTHHnDmfwwn7Th3ikHZZnsHYZb3lDxh9DjpmBSMuUWQilfpVTxvV1n126g==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/141492.Nicky_Cruz">About Nicky Cruz</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer2490082678258770602">Nicky was only 3½ years old when his heart turned to stone. As one of 18 children born to witchcraft-practicing parents from Puerto Rico, bloodshed and mayhem were common occurrences in his life. He suffered severe physical and mental abuse at their hands, at one time being declared the "Son of Satan" by his mother while she was in a spiritual trance.<br/><br/>When he was 15, Nicky's father sent him to visi</span>
  <span id="freeText2490082678258770602" style="display:none">Nicky was only 3½ years old when his heart turned to stone. As one of 18 children born to witchcraft-practicing parents from Puerto Rico, bloodshed and mayhem were common occurrences in his life. He suffered severe physical and mental abuse at their hands, at one time being declared the "Son of Satan" by his mother while she was in a spiritual trance.<br /><br />When he was 15, Nicky's father sent him to visit an older brother in New York. Nicky didn't stay with his brother long. Instead, full of anger and rage, he chose to make it on his own.<br /><br />Tough, but lonely, by age 16 he became a member of the notorious Brooklyn street gang known as the Mau Maus (named after a bloodthirsty African tribe). Within six months he became their president. Cruz fearlessly ruled the streets as warlord of one of the gangs most dreaded by rivals and police. Lost in the cycle of drugs, alcohol, and brutal violence, his life took a tragic turn for the worse after a friend and fellow gang member was horribly stabbed and beaten and died in Nicky's arms.<br /><br />As Cruz' reputation grew, so did his haunting nightmares. Arrested countless times, a court-ordered psychiatrist pronounced Nicky's fate as "headed to prison, the electric chair, and hell."<br /><br />No authority figure could reach Cruz - until he met a skinny street-preacher named <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/116175.David_R_Wilkerson" rel="nofollow noopener">David Wilkerson</a>. He disarmed Nicky - showing him something he'd never known before: Relentless love. His interest in the young thug was persistent. Nicky beat him up, spit on him and, on one occasion, seriously threatened his life, yet the love of God remained - stronger than any adversary Nicky had ever encountered.<br /><br />Finally, Wilkerson's presentation of the gospel message and the love of Jesus melted the thick walls of his heart. Nicky received the forgiveness, love and new life that can only come through Jesus. Since then, he has dedicated that life to helping others find the same freedom.<br /><br />He reaches today's youth because they relate to his background, trust his peer authority, and respond to the message of hope he delivers with both passion and conviction. <br /><br /><i>Run Baby Run</i> is Nicky's story in book form.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2490082678258770602" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
